Task instruction sent to agent 
# Dynamic AWS ECR Authentication for OCI Bundles

**Repository:** flipt-io/flipt
**Language:** Go
**Difficulty:** hard

## Problem

Flipt configured with OCI storage cannot continuously pull bundles from AWS ECR when using temporary credentials. Only static `username/password` authentication is supported today; AWS-issued tokens (e.g., via ECR) expire (commonly ~12h). After expiry, pulls to the OCI repository fail until credentials are manually rotated. A configuration-driven way to support non-static (provider-backed) authentication is needed so bundles continue syncing without manual intervention.

## Key Components

- `internal/oci/` — OCI storage implementation and authentication
- `cmd/flipt/` — bundle command handling
- `internal/storage/fs/` — filesystem storage layer
- Config schema — where OCI storage authentication options are defined

## Task

1. Add support for AWS credentials chain authentication in the OCI storage backend
2. Implement automatic token refresh so pulls continue succeeding across token expiries
3. Maintain backward compatibility with existing static `username/password` authentication
4. Add configuration option to select authentication type (static credentials vs. AWS provider chain)
5. Run existing tests to ensure no regressions

## Success Criteria

- OCI storage supports AWS credentials chain authentication
- Tokens refresh automatically before expiry
- Existing static credential authentication continues to work
- Configuration accepts the new authentication type
- All existing tests pass

    45→		}

     6→
     7→## Project Overview
     8→
     9→Flipt v2 is a Git-native feature management platform with a monorepo structure. This is the v2 version with a Git-native architecture.
    10→
    11→- **v1 code**: Located on `main` branch
    12→- **v2 code**: Located on current (`v2`) branch. This is the default branch in the repository.
    13→- **License**: Fair Core License for server, MIT for client code
    14→- **Requirements**: Go 1.25+ and Node.js 18+
    15→
    16→## Project Architecture & Structure
    17→
    18→### Repository Structure
    19→
    20→- `cmd/flipt/` - Main application entry point
    21→- `core/` - Core validation and business logic
    22→- `errors/` - Shared error definitions
    23→- `internal/` - Core application logic (not importable)
    24→  - `cmd/` - Internal command utilities and code generation tools
    25→  - `common/` - Shared types and utilities across internal packages
    26→  - `config/` - Configuration management
    27→  - `containers/` - Container test utilities
    28→  - `coss/` - Commercial open source features (license management, enterprise storage, secrets)
    29→  - `secrets/` - Secret management system with provider interface (OSS file provider, Pro Vault provider)
    30→  - `credentials/` - Credential management for cloud storage and Git authentication
    31→  - `ext/` - Import/export functionality for flags and segments
    32→  - `gateway/` - HTTP gateway implementation
    33→  - `info/` - Version and build information
    34→  - `migrations/` - Database

     1→# Flipt CLI TUI Design System
     2→
     3→This document outlines the design principles, patterns, and guidelines for building Terminal User Interface (TUI) components in the Flipt CLI. All interactive commands should follow these patterns to ensure a consistent and delightful user experience.
     4→
     5→## Table of Contents
     6→
     7→1. [Design Principles](#design-principles)
     8→2. [Color System](#color-system)
     9→3. [Typography and Styles](#typography-and-styles)
    10→4. [Layout System](#layout-system)
    11→5. [Component Patterns](#component-patterns)
    12→6. [Wizard Pattern](#wizard-pattern)
    13→7. [Forms and Input](#forms-and-input)
    14→8. [Progress Indicators](#progress-indicators)
    15→9. [Error Handling](#error-handling)
    16→10. [Success States](#success-states)
    17→11. [Code Examples](#code-examples)
    18→12. [Best Practices](#best-practices)
    19→
    20→## Design Principles
    21→
    22→### 1. Progressive Disclosure
    23→- Guide users through complex processes step-by-step
    24→- Reveal information and options as needed
    25→- Avoid overwhelming users with too many choices at once
    26→
    27→### 2. Clear Visual Hierarchy
    28→- Use badges, colors, and spacing to create clear information hierarchy
    29→- Most important information should be most prominent
    30→- Group related information together
    31→
    32→### 3. Responsive Design
    33→- Adapt to different terminal widths
    34→- Gracefully handle narrow terminals (minimum 48 characters)
    35→- Optimize for standard 80-character width
    36→
    37→### 4. Consistent Experience
    38→- All commands should feel like part of the same product
    39→- Reuse patterns and components across commands
    40→- Maintain consistent spacing and
... (truncated)

   200→// SSHAuth provides configuration support for SSH private key credentials when
   201→// authenticating with private git repositories
   202→type SSHAuth struct {
   203→	User                  string `json:"-" mapstructure:"user" yaml:"-" `
   204→	Password              string `json:"-" mapstructure:"password" yaml:"-" `
   205→	PrivateKeyBytes       string `json:"-" mapstructure:"private_key_bytes" yaml:"-" `
   206→	PrivateKeyPath        string `json:"-" mapstructure:"private_key_path" yaml:"-" `
   207→	InsecureIgnoreHostKey bool   `json:"-" mapstructure:"insecure_ignore_host_key" yaml:"-"`
   208→}
   209→
   210→func (a SSHAuth) validate() (err error) {
   211→	defer func() {
   212→		if err != nil {
   213→			err = fmt.Errorf("ssh authentication: %w", err)
   214→		}
   215→	}()
   216→
   217→	if a.Password == "" {
   218→		return errors.New("password required")
   219→	}
   220→
   221→	if (a.PrivateKeyBytes == "" && a.PrivateKeyPath == "") || (a.PrivateKeyBytes != "" && a.PrivateKeyPath != "") {
   222→		return errors.New("please provide exclusively one of private_key_bytes or private_key_path")
   223→	}
   224→
   225→	return nil
   226→}

   229→	Repository string `json:"repository,omitempty" mapstructure:"repository" yaml:"repository,omitempty"`

    16→type S3ClientAPI interface {
    17→	ListObjectsV2(context.Context, *s3.ListObjectsV2Input, ...func(*s3.Options)) (*s3.ListObjectsV2Output, error)

    21→// FS is only for accessing files in a single bucket. The directory
    22→// entries are cached. It is specifically intended for use by a source
    23→// that calls fs.WalkDir and does not fully implement all fs operations
    24→type FS struct {
    25→	logger   *zap.Logger
    26→	s3Client S3ClientAPI
    27→
    28→	// configuration
    29→	bucket string
    30→	prefix string
    31→
    32→	// cached entries
    33→	dirEntry *Dir
    34→}
    35→
    36→// ensure FS implements fs.FS aka Open
    37→var _ fs.FS = &FS{}
    38→
    39→// ensure FS implements fs.StatFS aka Stat
    40→var _ fs.StatFS = &FS{}
    41→
    42→// ensure FS implements fs.ReadDirFS aka ReadDir
    43→var _ fs.ReadDirFS = &FS{}
    44→
    45→// New creates a FS for the single bucket
    46→func New(logger *zap.Logger, s3Client S3ClientAPI, bucket string, prefix string) (*FS, error) {
    47→	return &FS{
    48→		logger:   logger,
    49→		s3Client: s3Client,
    50→		bucket:   bucket,
    51→		prefix:   prefix,
    52→	}, nil
    53→}

    20→// Source is an implementation of storage/fs.FSSource
    21→// This implementation is backed by a Git repository and it tracks an upstream reference.
    22→// When subscribing to this source, the upstream reference is tracked
    23→// by polling the upstream on a configurable interval.
    24→type Source struct {
    25→	logger *zap.Logger
    26→	repo   *git.Repository
    27→

    29→	ref      string
    30→	hash     plumbing.Hash
    31→	interval time.Duration
    32→	auth     transport.AuthMethod
    33→}
    34→
    35→// WithRef configures the target reference to be used when fetching
    36→// and building fs.FS implementations.
    37→// If it is a valid hash, then the fixed SHA value is used.
    38→// Otherwise, it is treated as a reference in the origin upstream.
    39→func WithRef(ref string) containers.Option[Source] {
    40→	return func(s *Source) {
    41→		if plumbing.IsHash(ref) {
    42→			s.hash = plumbing.NewHash(ref)
    43→			return
    44→		}
    45→
    46→		s.ref = ref
    47→	}
    48→}
    49→
    50→// WithPollInterval configures the interval in which origin is polled to
    51→// discover any updates to the target reference.
    52→func WithPollInterval(tick time.Duration) containers.Option[Source] {
    53→	ret

    12→// FSSource produces implementations of fs.FS.
    13→// A single FS can be produced via Get or a channel
    14→// may be provided to Subscribe in order to received
    15→// new instances when new state becomes available.
    16→type FSSource interface {
    17→	fmt.Stringer
    18→
    19→	// Get builds a single instance of an fs.FS
    20→	Get() (fs.FS, error)
    21→
    22→	// Subscribe feeds implementations of fs.FS onto the provided channel.
    23→	// It should block until the provided context is cancelled (it will be called in a goroutine).
    24→	// It should close the provided channel before it returns.
    25→	Subscribe(context.Context, chan<- fs.FS)
    26→}
    27→
    28→// Store is an implementation of storage.Store backed by an FSSource.
    29→// The store subscribes to the source for instances of fs.FS with new contents.
    30→// When a new fs is received the contents is fetched and built into a snapshot
    31→// of Flipt feature flag state.
    32→type Store struct {
    33→	*syncedStore
    34→
    35→	logger *zap.Logger
    36→	source FSSource
    37→
    38→	// notify is used for test purposes
    39→	// it is invoked if defined when a snapshot update finishes
    40→	notify func()
    41→
    42→	cancel context.CancelFunc
    43→	done   chan struct{}
    44→}
    45→
    46→func (l *Store) updateSnapshot(fs fs.FS) error {
    47→	storeSnapshot, err := SnapshotFromFS(l.logger, fs)
    48→	if err != nil {
    49→		return err
    50→	}
    51→
    52→	l.mu.Lock()
    53→	l.Store = storeSnapshot
    54→	l.mu.Unlock()
    55→

    18→func newBunchCommand() *cobra.Command {
    19→	bunch := &bunchCommand{}
    20→
    21→	cmd := &cobra.Command{
    22→		Use:   "bunch",
    23→		Short: "Manage flipt bunches",
    24→	}
    25→

    27→		Use:   "list",
    28→		Short: "list all bunches",
    29→		RunE:  bunch.list,
    30→	})
    31→
    32→	cmd.AddCommand(&cobra.Command{
    33→		Use:   "create",
    34→		Short: "create a bunch",
    35→		RunE:  bunch.create,
    36→	})
    37→
    38→	cmd.AddCommand(&cobra.Command{
    39→		Use:   "push",
    40→		Short: "push a bunch",
    41→		RunE:  bunch.push,
    42→		Args:  cobra.ExactArgs(1),
    43→	})
    44→
    45→	cmd.AddCommand(&cobra.Command{
    46→		Use:   "pull",
    47→		Short: "pull a bunch",
    48→		RunE:  bunch.pull,
    49→		Args:  cobra.ExactArgs(1),
    50→	})
    51→
    52→	return cmd
    53→}
    54→
    55→func (c *bunchCommand) list(cmd *cobra.Command, args []string) error {
    56→	store, err := getStore()
    57→	if err != nil {
    58→		return err
    59→	}
    60→
    61→	bunches, err := store.List()
    62→	if err != nil {
    63→		return err
    64→	}
    65→
    66→	wr := writer()
    67→
    68→	fmt.Fprintf(wr, "DIGEST\tREPO\tTAG\tCREATED\t\n")
    69→	for _, bunch := range bunches {
    70→		fmt.Fprintf(wr, "%s\t%s\t%s\t%s\t\n", bunch.Digest.Hex()[:7], bunch.Repository, bunch.Tag, bunch.CreatedAt)
    71→	}
    72→
    73→	return wr.Flush()
    74→}

     1→package fs
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"context"

     6→	"io/fs"
     7→	"path"
     8→
     9→	"go.uber.org/zap"
    10→)
    11→
    12→// FSSource produces implementations of fs.FS.
    13→// A single FS can be produced via Get or a channel
    14→// may be provided to Subscribe in order to received
    15→// new instances when new state becomes available.
    16→type FSSource interface {
    17→	fmt.Stringer
    18→
    19→	// Get builds a single instance of an fs.FS
    20→	Get() (fs.FS, error)
    21→
    22→	// Subscribe feeds implementations of fs.FS onto the provided channel.
    23→	// It should block until the provided context is cancelled (it will be called in a goroutine).
    24→	// It should close the provided channel before it returns.
    25→	Subscribe(context.Context, chan<- fs.FS)
    26→}
    27→
    28→// Store is an implementation of storage.Store backed by an FSSource.
    29→// The store subscribes to the source for instances of fs.FS with new contents.
    30→// When a new fs is received the contents is fetched and built into a snapshot
    31→// of Flipt feature flag state.
    32→type Store struct {
    33→	*syncedStore
    34→
    35→	logger *zap.Logger
    36→	source FSSource
    37→
    38→	// notify is used for test purposes
    39→	// it is invoked if defined when a snapshot update finishes
    40→	notify func()
    41→
    42→	cancel context.CancelFunc
    43→	done   chan struct{}
    44→}
    45→
    46→func (l *Store) updateSnapshot(fs fs.FS) error {
    47→	storeSnapshot, err := SnapshotFromFS(l.logger, fs)
    48→	if err != nil {
    49→		return err
    50→	}
    51→
    52→	l.mu.Lock()
    53→	l.Store = storeSnapshot
    54→	l.mu.Unlock()
    55→
    56→	// NOTE: this is really just a trick for unit tests
  
... (truncated)

    40→	}

    46→}

    48→// Subscribe feeds local fs.FS implementations onto the provided channel.
    49→// It blocks until the provided context is cancelled.
    50→func (s *Source) Subscribe(ctx context.Context, ch chan<- fs.FS) {
    51→	defer close(ch)

    56→		case <-ctx.Done():
    57→			return
    58→		case <-ticker.C:
    59→			fs, err := s.Get()
    60→			if err != nil {
    61→				s.logger.Error("error getting file system from directory", zap.Error(err))
    62→				continue
    63→			}

     3→// Option is any function which receives a pointer to any type T.
     4→type Option[T any] func(*T)
     5→
     6→// ApplyAll takes a pointer to type T and it passes it onto each supplied Option
     7→// function in the supplied order.
     8→func ApplyAll[T any](t *T, opts ...Option[T]) {
     9→	for _, opt := range opts {
    10→		opt(t)
    11→	}
    12→}

# Authentication in ORAS

Based on the provided documentation, specific details about ORAS authentication types are not covered in this introduction page. 

The content only mentions that "It allows you to push (upload) and pull (download) things to and from an OCI Registry, and also handles login (authentication) and token flow (authorization)."

This is the v2 version with a Git-native architecture.\n\n- **v1 code**: Located on `main` branch\n- **v2 code**: Located on current (`v2`) branch. This is the default branch in the repository.\n- **License**: Fair Core License for server, MIT for client code\n- **Requirements**: Go 1.25+ and Node.js 18+\n\n## Project Architecture & Structure\n\n### Repository Structure\n\n- `cmd/flipt/` - Main application entry point\n- `core/` - Core validation and business logic\n- `errors/` - Shared error definitions\n- `internal/` - Core application logic (not importable)\n  - `cmd/` - Internal command utilities and code generation tools\n  - `common/` - Shared types and utilities across internal packages\n  - `config/` - Configuration management\n  - `containers/` - Container test utilities\n  - `coss/` - Commercial open source features (license management, enterprise storage, secrets)\n  - `secrets/` - Secret management system with provider interface (OSS file provider, Pro Vault provider)\n  - `credentials/` - Credential management for cloud storage and Git authentication\n  - `ext/` - Import/export functionality for flags and segments\n  - `gateway/` - HTTP gateway implementation\n  - `info/` - Version and build information\n  - `migrations/` - Database migration files (ClickHouse for analytics)\n  - `otel/` - OpenTelemetry integration (logs, metrics, traces)\n  - `product/` - Product metadata and feature flags\n  - `release/` - Release version checking\n  - `server/` - gRPC and HTTP server implementations\n    - `analytics/` - Analytics collection server (Prometheus, ClickHouse)\n    - `authn/` - Authentication server and middleware\n    - `authz/` - Authorization server with Rego engine\n    - `environments/` - `analytics/` - Analytics data storage\n    - `authn/` - Authentication storage (Redis, memory, static)\n    - `environments/` - Environment-aware storage with Git support\n    - `fs/` - File system abstraction layer\n    - `git/` - Git repository management\n  - `telemetry/` - Usage telemetry collection\n- `rpc/` - Protocol buffer definitions and generated code\n  - `flipt/` - Main Flipt API (v1)\n  - `v2/` - V2 APIs (environments, analytics, evaluation)\n- `sdk/` - Client SDKs (Go SDK included)\n- `ui/` - React/TypeScript frontend\n\n### Key Components\n\n#### Storage Layer\n\nMulti-backend storage supporting:\n\n- Git repositories (primary for v2)\n- File system (local development)\n- Cloud storage (S3, GCS, Azure Blob) - Flipt config only\n\n#### Environments System\n\n- Environment-per-branch: Map Git branches to environments\n- Environment-per-directory: Organize by microservice/team\n- Environment-per-repository: Separate repos for products\n\n#### APIs\n\n- gRPC API (port 9000) - Primary interface\n- REST API (port 8080) - HTTP gateway over gRPC\n- OpenFeature compatible evaluation\n\n##### Key Endpoints\n\n- **Evaluation API**: `/api/v1/evaluate` - Evaluate feature flags\n- **Management API**: Full CRUD operations on flags, segments, rules\n- **Analytics API**: `/api/v2/analytics` - Flag evaluation metrics\n- **Environments API**: `/api/v2/environments` - Environment management\n- **OFREP API**: `/ofrep/v1` - OpenFeature Remote Evaluation Protocol\n\n#### UI Architecture\n\n- React 19 with TypeScript\n- Redux Toolkit for state management\n- Tailwind CSS for styling\n- Vite for build tooling\n- React Router for navigation\n\n## Development Setup & Commands\n\n### Initial Setup\n\n```bash\n# Install required development tools\nmage bootstrap\n```\n\n### Development Workflow\n\n1. **Setup**: Run `mage bootstrap` to install tools\n2. **Backend Development**:\n   - Use `mage go:run` for server\n   - Server runs on port 8080 (HTTP) and 9000 (gRPC)\n3. **Frontend Development**:\n   - Run `mage ui:run` for UI dev server on port 5173\n   - UI proxies API requests to backend on port 8080\n4. **Full Development**: Run both servers simultaneously\n\n### Build & Run Commands\n\n- `mage build` - Builds the project similar to a release build (default target)\n- `mage go:build` - Builds Go server for development without bundling assets\n- `mage go:run` - Runs Go server in development mode with local config\n- `mage dev` - Alias for go:run\n- `./bin/flipt server --config config/local.yml` - Run built binary with local config\n\n### UI Development Commands\n\n- `mage ui:deps` - Install UI dependencies\n- `mage ui:run` - Run UI in development mode (port 5173)\n- `mage ui:dev` - Alias for ui:run\n- `mage ui:build` - Build UI assets for release\n- `cd ui && npm run dev` - Alternative way to run UI dev server\n\n### Testing Commands\n\n- `mage go:test` - Run all Go unit tests\n- `go test -v {path} -run {test}` - Run a specific Go test\n- `mage go:bench` - Run Go benchmarking tests\n- `mage go:cover` - Run tests and generate coverage report\n- `cd ui && npm run test` - Run UI unit tests (Jest)\n\n### Code Quality Commands\n\n- `mage go:lint` - Run Go linters (golangci-lint and buf lint)\n- `mage go:fmt` - Format Go code with goimports\n- `mage ui:lint` - Run UI linters (ESLint)\n- `mage ui:fmt` - Format UI code (Prettier)\n\n### Code Generation Commands\n\n- `mage go:proto` - Generate protobuf files and gRPC stubs\n- `mage go:mockery` - Generate mocks\n- `mage go:generate` - Generate both mocks and proto files\n\n### Cleanup Commands\n\n- `mage clean` - Clean built files and tidy go.mod\n- `mage prep` - Prepare project for building (clean + ui:build)\n\n### Build Process Notes\n\n- Protocol buffers generate Go and gateway code\n- Mockery generates Go test mocks. See .mockery.yml\n- UI has no code generation\n\n## Code Style Guidelines\n\n### Go Code Style\n\n#### Foundation: Google Go Style Guide\n\n**All Go code should follow the [Google Go Style Guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/go/guide) as the base style guide.**\n\nThe guidelines below are Flipt-specific conventions that build upon the Google style guide. When in doubt, refer to the Google guide first, then apply these project-specific patterns.\n\nKey areas from the Google guide to pay special attention to:\n\n- **Formatting**: Use `gofmt` (we use `goimports` which includes `gofmt`)\n- **Naming**: Follow Go naming conventions for packages, types, functions, and variables\n- **Package organization**: Keep packages focused and avoid circular dependencies\n- **Error handling**: Return errors as the last return value, handle errors explicitly\n- **Documentation**: Write clear godoc comments for exported types and functions\n\n#### Naming Conventions\n\n- **Public functions**: Use PascalCase (`NewServer`, `ListFlags`, `RegisterGRPC`)\n- **Private functions**: Use camelCase (`getStore`, `buildConfig`, `handleError`)\n- **Factory functions**: Use `New` prefix for constructors (`NewRepository`, `NewEnvironmentFactory`)\n- **Variables**: Use camelCase (`environmentKey`, `namespaceKey`, `startTime`)\n- **Constants**: Use PascalCase for exported, camelCase for unexported\n- **Interfaces**: Use descriptive names (`Store`, `EnvironmentStore`, `Validator`)\n\n#### Variable Declarations\n\n```go\n// Prefer := for single variable declarations\nresult := SomeType{}\n\n// Use var blocks for multiple related variables\nvar (\n    environmentKey = r.EnvironmentKey\n    namespaceKey   = r.NamespaceKey\n    startTime      = time.Now().UTC()\n)\n```\n\n#### Constants\n\nUse constants when appropriate for values that are unlikely to change. Even in tests.\n\n**\u274c Bad Examples**\n\n```go\nvar (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n```go\n  maxRetries := 3\n  secretProvider := \"vault\"\n```\n\n**\u2705 Good Example**\n\n```go\nconst (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Error Handling\n\n##### Error Types\n\nUse the custom error types when possible:\n\n```go\n// Preferred - use custom error types\nreturn nil, errs.ErrNotFoundf(\"flag %q not found\", key)\nreturn nil, errs.ErrInvalidf(\"invalid configuration: %s\", reason)\n\n// Fallback - standard error handling\nreturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to process: %w\", err)\n```\n\n##### Inline Errors\n\nPrefer inline error declarations and checking when it makes sense.\n\n**\u274c Bad Example**\n\n```go\nerr := doSomething()\nif err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**\u2705 Good Example**\n\n```go\nif err := doSomething(); err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Imports\n\nFollow the three-group import pattern (extends Google guide):\n\n```go\nimport (\n    // Standard library\n    \"context\"\n    \"fmt\"\n    \"time\"\n\n    // Third-party packages\n    \"github.com/go-git/go-git/v6\"\n    \"go.uber.org/zap\"\n\n    // Local packages\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/errors\"\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Logging\n\nUse structured logging with zap:\n\n```go\n// Preferred - structured logging with context\ns.logger.Debug(\"processing request\", \n    zap.String(\"environment\", envKey),\n    zap.String(\"namespace\", nsKey),\n    zap.Int(\"count\", len(items)))\n\n// Use appropriate log levels\ns.logger.Debug(\"debug info for development\")  // Most common\ns.logger.Info(\"important application events\")\ns.logger.Warn(\"recoverable error conditions\")\ns.logger.Error(\"error conditions that need attention\")\n\n// Avoid overusing log statements - be selective about what to log\n```\n\n#### Comments and Documentation\n\n```go\n// Public functions need godoc comments starting with function name\n// ListFlags lists all flags in the specified environment and namespace\nfunc (s *Server) ListFlags(ctx context.Context, r *flipt.ListFlagRequest) (*flipt.FlagList, error) {\n    // Inline comments explain complex logic\n    // Check for X-Environment header for backward compatibility\n    environmentKey := r.EnvironmentKey\n    if headerEnv, ok := common.FliptEnvironmentFromContext(ctx); ok && headerEnv != \"\" {\n        environmentKey = headerEnv\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Project Organization\n\n- Use `internal/` for private packages that shouldn't be imported externally\n- Organize by domain (`server/`, `storage/`, `config/`, `analytics/`)\n- Keep interfaces in domain root, implementations in subdirectories\n- Co-locate tests with implementation (`*_test.go`)\n- Use `testdata/` directories for test fixtures\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (Go)\n\n**Always run these commands when adding or editing Go code:**\n\n```bash\n# Format Go code\nmage go:fmt\n\n# Lint Go code\nmage go:lint\n\n# Run modernize to update code to 1.24+ style\nmage go:modernize\n```\n\n### UI/React/TypeScript Code Style\n\n#### File Naming and Organization\n\n- **Components**: Use PascalCase for `.tsx` files (`FlagForm.tsx`, `FlagTable.tsx`)\n- **API files**: Use camelCase with suffix (`flagsApi.ts`, `authApi.ts`)\n- **Types**: Use PascalCase for `.ts` files (`Flag.ts`, `Analytics.ts`)\n- **Utilities**: Use descriptive lowercase names (`helpers.ts`)\n\n#### Component Structure\n\n- Use functional components with hooks\n- Organize components by domain in directories\n- Keep reusable UI components in `ui/` directory\n- Co-locate component tests with implementation\n\n#### State Management\n\n- Use Redux Toolkit for application state\n- Create API slices for domain-specific data (`flagsApi.ts`)\n- Use TypeScript for type safety throughout\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (UI)\n\n**Always run these commands when adding or editing UI code:**\n\n```bash\n# Format UI code (TypeScript/React)\nmage ui:fmt\n\n# Lint UI code (ESLint)\nmage ui:lint\n```\n\n### General Pre-commit Checks\n\n```bash\n# Format specific markdown files (replace with actual filename)\nnpx prettier -w README.md\n```\n\n## Configuration\n\n### Configuration Files\n\n- `config/local.yml` - Local development config\n- `config/dev.yml` - Alternative dev config\n- User config at `{{ USER_CONFIG_DIR }}/flipt/config.yml`\n\n### Debugging Tips\n\n- Use `FLIPT_LOG_LEVEL=debug` for verbose and Playwright for E2E\n\n### Writing Effective Tests\n\nWhen writing tests, ensure they actually verify the functionality being tested:\n\n**\u274c Bad Example - Test doesn't verify actual behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test only verifies the method runs without error, not that the logic works\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    assert.NotNil(t, result)\n}\n```\n\n**\u2705 Good Example - Test verifies specific behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test verifies the actual logic and behavior\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Use mock.MatchedBy to verify the correct data is passed through\n    store.On(\"Method\", mock.MatchedBy(func(ctx context.Context) bool {\n        // Verify the context contains the expected values\n        value, ok := somePackage.ValueFromContext(ctx)\n        return ok && value == expectedValue\n    }), expectedArg).Return(expectedResult, nil)\n    \n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    \n    // Verify the actual business logic worked correctly\n    assert.Equal(t, expectedOutput, result.ImportantField)\n    store.AssertExpectations(t) // Ensures mocks were called as expected\n}\n```\n\n**Key Testing Principles:**\n\n- **Verify behavior, not just success**: Don't just check that methods return without error\n- **Test the logic**: Use `mock.MatchedBy` to verify correct data flows through the system\n- **Test edge cases**: Include tests for when conditions are met vs. not met\n- **Use meaningful assertions**: Assert on the specific values that matter to the business logic\n- **Mock verification**: Use `mock.AssertExpectations(t)` to ensure mocks were called with expected parameters\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nIntegration tests are defined in `build/testing/` and run as Mage targets. For details on available integration test targets, helpers, and how to add new integration tests, see the files in that directory:\n\n- `build/testing/integration.go` - Integration test Mage targets and configuration\n- `build/testing/integration/` - Individual integration test suites\n- `build/testing/helpers.go` - Shared test helpers\n- `build/testing/test.go` - Core test utilities\n\n## Git Workflow & Commits\n\n### Creating Effective Commits\n\n#### Commit Message Format\n\nFollow conventional commit format:\n\n```\ntype(scope): brief description\n\nLonger description if needed explaining the why, not the what.\n\n- List specific changes if helpful\n- Include any breaking changes\n- Reference issues (e.g., \"Fixes #123\")\n```\n\n#### Commit Types\n\n- `feat:` - New features\n- `fix:` - Bug fixes\n- `docs:` - Documentation changes\n- `style:` - Code style changes (formatting, etc.)\n- `refactor:` - Code refactoring without functional changes\n- `test:` - Adding or modifying tests\n- `chore:` - Build process or auxiliary tool changes\n\n#### Examples\n\n```bash\n# Good commit messages\ngit commit -s -m \"feat: add X-Environment header support to ListFlags endpoint\n\nThe v1 ListFlags endpoint now checks for X-Environment header \nfor backward compatibility. Similarly for a v1 (main) feature, use the `v1` label.\n\n#### Quality Checklist\n\nBefore creating a PR, ensure:\n\n- [ ] Code follows style guidelines\n- [ ] Tests are added and passing\n- [ ] Linting passes (`mage go:lint` / `mage ui:lint`)\n- [ ] Code is formatted (`mage go:fmt` / `mage ui:fmt`)\n- [ ] Commit messages are clear and descriptive\n- [ ] PR description explains the change and its purpose\n",

Progressive Disclosure\n- Guide users through complex processes step-by-step\n- Reveal information and options as needed\n- Avoid overwhelming users with too many choices at once\n\n### 2. Clear Visual Hierarchy\n- Use badges, colors, and spacing to create clear information hierarchy\n- Most important information should be most prominent\n- Group related information together\n\n### 3. Responsive Design\n- Adapt to different terminal widths\n- Gracefully handle narrow terminals (minimum 48 characters)\n- Optimize for standard 80-character width\n\n### 4. Consistent Experience\n- All commands should feel like part of the same product\n- Reuse patterns and components across commands\n- Maintain consistent spacing and alignment\n\n### 5.   "prompt": "What authentication methods are supported in ORAS Go? How do I authenticate a remote.Repository?",
  "url": "https://pkg.go.dev/oras.land/oras-go/v2@v2.3.1"

Output
"# Authentication Methods in ORAS Go\n\nBased on the documentation, ORAS Go supports authentication for remote repositories through the `registry/remote/auth` package.\n\n## Supported Authentication Methods\n\nThe primary authentication mechanism is via the **`auth.Client`** which provides:\n\n1. **Static Credentials** - The most straightforward method using username/password pairs\n2. **Credential Cache** - Built-in caching to avoid repeated authentication\n3. **Custom Credential Providers** - Extensible system for implementing custom authentication logic\n\n## How to Authenticate a Remote Repository\n\nHere's the standard pattern from the documentation examples:\n\n```go\nimport (\n    \"oras.land/oras-go/v2/registry/remote\"\n    \"oras.land/oras-go/v2/registry/remote/auth\"\n    \"oras.land/oras-go/v2/registry/remote/retry\"\n)\n\n// Connect to a remote repository\nreg := \"myregistry.example.com\"\nrepo, err := remote.NewRepository(reg + \"/myrepo\")\nif err != nil {\n    panic(err)\n}\n\n// Configure authentication\nrepo.Client = &auth.Client{\n    Client: retry.DefaultClient,\n    Cache:  auth.DefaultCache,\n    Credential: auth.StaticCredential(reg, auth.Credential{\n        Username: \"username\",\n        Password: \"password\",\n    }),\n}\n```\n\n## Key Components\n\n- **`auth.Client`** - Wraps HTTP client with authentication support\n- **`retry.DefaultClient`** - Handles retries with exponential backoff\n- **`auth.DefaultCache`** - Caches credentials to improve performance\n- **`auth.StaticCredential()`** - Creates static username/password credentials\n- **`auth.Credential`** - Struct containing Username and Password fields\n\nThe authentication is applied at the HTTP client level, so all subsequent registry operations through that repository will use the configured credentials."

"# Credential Types and Authentication Methods in the Auth Package\n\nBased on the documentation, the `auth` package provides the following credential types and authentication methods:\n\n## Credential Types\n\nThe `Credential` struct supports multiple authentication approaches:\n\n```go\ntype Credential struct {\n    Username string      // Username for the remote registry\n    Password string      // Password associated with username\n    RefreshToken string  // Bearer token for fetching access tokens (OAuth2)\n    AccessToken string   // Bearer token to send directly to registry\n}\n```\n\n## Authentication Schemes\n\nThe package defines three authentication schemes:\n\n1. **SchemeBasic** - HTTP Basic authentication (RFC 7617)\n2. **SchemeBearer** - Bearer token authentication (OAuth 2.0, RFC 6750)\n3. **SchemeUnknown** - Unknown or unsupported schemes\n\n## Supported Authentication Methods\n\nThe `Client` type supports the following authentication patterns:\n\n### 1. **Basic Authentication** (Username/Password)\n```go\nclient := &auth.Client{\n    Credential: auth.StaticCredential(expectedHostAddress, auth.Credential{\n        Username: username,\n        Password: password,\n    }),\n}\n```\n\n### 2. **Access Token**\n```go\nclient := &auth.Client{\n    Credential: auth.StaticCredential(expectedHostAddress, auth.Credential{\n        AccessToken: accessToken,\n    }),\n}\n```\n\n### 3. **Refresh Token** (OAuth2)\n```go\nclient := &auth.Client{\n    Credential: auth.StaticCredential(expectedHostAddress, auth.Credential{\n        RefreshToken: refreshToken,\n    }),\n}\n```\n\n### 4. **OAuth2 Password Grant**\nThe `Client` has a `ForceAttemptOAuth2` field to enforce OAuth2 authentication instead of the distribution spec when using username and password.\n\n## Key Features\n\n- **Caching**: Built-in `Cache` interface for storing authentication tokens\n- **Scopes**: Support for Docker registry authentication scopes (pull, push, delete)\n- **User Agent**: Customizable user agent via `SetUserAgent()`\n- **Static Credentials**: `StaticCredential()` helper for specifying credentials per registry"

{
  "prompt": "What are the examples for using auth with ORAS remote repositories?",
  "url": "https://pkg.go.dev/oras.land/oras-go/v2@v2.3.1/registry/remote/auth#hdr-Examples"

"# Examples for Using Auth with ORAS Remote Repositories\n\nBased on the documentation, here are the five main examples provided for the `auth.Client.Do()` method:\n\n## 1. **BasicAuth** - Username and Password\n```go\nclient := &auth.Client{\n\tCredential: auth.StaticCredential(expectedHostAddress, auth.Credential{\n\t\tUsername: username,\n\t\tPassword: password,\n\t}),\n}\nreq, err := http.NewRequest(http.MethodGet, basicAuthTargetURL, nil)\nresp, err := client.Do(req)\n```\n\n## 2. **WithAccessToken** - Bearer Token\n```go\nclient := &auth.Client{\n\tCredential: auth.StaticCredential(expectedHostAddress, auth.Credential{\n\t\tAccessToken: accessToken,\n\t}),\n}\nreq, err := http.NewRequest(http.MethodGet, accessTokenTargetURL, nil)\nresp, err := client.Do(req)\n```\n\n## 3. **WithRefreshToken** - OAuth2 Identity Token\n```go\nclient := &auth.Client{\n\tCredential: auth.StaticCredential(expectedHostAddress, auth.Credential{\n\t\tRefreshToken: refreshToken,\n\t}),\n}\nreq, err := http.NewRequest(http.MethodGet, refreshTokenTargetURL, nil)\nresp, err := client.Do(req)\n```\n\n## 4. **MinimalClient** - No Credentials\n```go\nvar client auth.Client\nreq, err := http.NewRequest(http.MethodGet, targetURL, nil)\nresp, err := client.Do(req)\n```\n\n## 5. **ClientConfigurations** - Advanced Options\n```go\nclient := &auth.Client{\n\tCredential: auth.StaticCredential(expectedHostAddress, auth.Credential{\n\t\tUsername: username,\n\t\tPassword: password,\n\t}),\n\tForceAttemptOAuth2: true,\n\tCache: auth.NewCache(),\n}\nclient.SetUserAgent(\"example user agent\")\n\nscopes := []string{\n\t\"repository:dst:pull,push\",\n\t\"repository:src:pull\",\n}\nctx := auth.WithScopes(context.Background(), scopes...)\nreq, err := http.NewRequestWithContext(ctx, http.MethodGet, clientConfigTargetURL, nil)\nresp, err := client.Do(req)\n```\n\nThe auth package supports multiple credential types and authentication schemes (Basic and Bearer token) for accessing remote registries."

Input
{
  "content": "# Implementation Plan: Dynamic AWS ECR Authentication for OCI Bundles\n\n## Context\n\n**Problem**: Flipt configured with OCI storage cannot continuously pull bundles from AWS ECR when using temporary credentials. Only static `username/password` authentication is supported today; AWS-issued tokens expire (~12h), and after expiry, pulls fail until credentials are manually rotated.\n\n**Solution Approach**: Add support for AWS credentials chain authentication in OCI storage, with automatic token refresh through periodic re-pulling (leveraging existing polling infrastructure).\n\n**Scope**:\n- Add authentication configuration options to OCI storage (static + AWS provider chain)\n- Implement AWS ECR authentication using AWS SDK v2\n- Leverage existing polling mechanism for automatic token refresh\n- Maintain backward compatibility with static credentials\n- Follow established Flipt patterns (Git storage auth as a model)\n\n---\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\n### Phase 1: Configuration Changes\n**File**: `internal/config/storage.go`\n\n1. **Extend OCI struct** to include authentication options (following Git storage pattern):\n   - Add `Authentication` field to OCI struct\n   - Define `OCIAuthentication` struct with:\n     - `BasicAuth` (*BasicAuth) - for static username/password or ECR static credentials\n     - `TokenAuth` (*TokenAuth) - for bearer tokens\n     - `AWSAuth` (*AWSAuth) - NEW, for AWS credential chain (ECR)\n\n2. **Define AWSAuth struct** with:\n   ```go\n   type AWSAuth struct {\n       Region       string  // Optional, auto-detected if not provided\n       UseChain     bool    // If true, use AWS credential chain (env vars, IAM role, etc.)\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Add validation** for auth exclusivity (only one auth type at a time)\n\n4. **Add setDefaults** for OCI polling interval (similar to S3)\n\n### Phase 2: OCI Source Authentication Support\n**File**: `internal/storage/fs/oci/source.go`\n\n1. **Extend Source struct** to store auth:\n   - Add `auth *oras.auth.Client` field (or use ORAS's auth mechanism)\n   - Keep reference to auth credentials for refresh on poll\n\n2. **Implement WithAuth() option function**:\n   ```go\n   func WithAuth(auth AuthProvider) containers.Option[Source]\n   func WithAWSAuth(region string) containers.Option[Source]\n   func WithBasicAuth(username, password string) containers.Option[Source]\n   ```\n\n3. **Create AuthProvider interface** to abstract different auth implementations:\n   ```go\n   type AuthProvider interface {\n       GetCredential(ctx context.Context, hostname string) (auth.Credential, error)\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Implement AWS auth provider**:\n   - Use AWS SDK v2 `config.LoadDefaultConfig()` for credential chain\n   - Implement GetECRAuthorizationToken() for pulling ECR authorization tokens\n   - Handle token caching with configurable TTL\n\n5. **Update NewSource()** to:\n   - Accept auth options\n   - Build ORAS `auth.Client` from AuthProvider\n   - Set client on remote.Repository\n\n6. **Update Subscribe()** (polling mechanism) to:\n   - Refresh credentials on each poll interval (automatic token refresh)\n   - This leverages existing polling - no new infrastructure needed\n\n### Phase 3: Server Initialization\n**File**: `internal/cmd/grpc.go`\n\n1. **Add OCI auth handling** in the storage initialization section (around lines 224-233):\n   - Parse OCI authentication from config\n   - Create AuthProvider based on auth type:\n     - BasicAuth \u2192 static credential provider\n     - AWSAuth \u2192 AWS credential chain provider\n   - Pass auth options to `oci.NewSource()`\n\n2. **Follow Git auth pattern** (lines 160-198) but adapted for OCI:\n   ```go\n   if cfg.Storage.OCI.Authentication.BasicAuth != nil {\n       opts = append(opts, oci.WithBasicAuth(...))\n   }\n   if cfg.Storage.OCI.Authentication.AWSAuth != nil {\n       opts = append(opts, oci.WithAWSAuth(...))\n   }\n   ```\n\n### Phase 4: OCI Store Updates\n**Files**: `internal/oci/store.go`, `internal/storage/fs/oci/source.go`\n\n1. **Push/Pull operations** should use authenticated repositories:\n   - Update `Push()` method to use auth from Source\n   - Update `Pull()` method to use auth from Source\n   - Pass remote.Repository with auth client to oras.Copy()\n\n2. **Token refresh mechanism**:\n   - Leverage Subscribe() polling - each poll calls Get() which re-evaluates credentials\n   - AWS SDK handles credential caching and refresh automatically\n   - No explicit token refresh code needed\n\n### Phase 5: Testing & Validation\n**Files**: Create/update test files\n\n1. **Unit tests** for:\n   - OCI config validation (mutually exclusive auth types)\n   - AWS auth provider credential fetching (mocked)\n   - Static auth provider creation\n\n2. **Integration tests** for:\n   - Push/Pull with static credentials\n   - Push/Pull with AWS auth (mocked AWS SDK)\n   - Token refresh behavior (verify re-auth on poll)\n\n---\n\n## Critical Implementation Files\n\n| File | Changes | Purpose |\n|------|---------|---------|\n| `internal/config/storage.go` | Add OCI authentication fields, AWSAuth struct, validation | Configuration structure |\n| `internal/storage/fs/oci/source.go` | Add auth support, options, AuthProvider interface, AWS integration | OCI source with auth |\n| `internal/cmd/grpc.go` | Add OCI auth initialization (lines ~224-233) | Dependency injection/setup |\n| `internal/oci/store.go` | Update Push/Pull to use auth from source | OCI operations |\n| `internal/oci/fs/fs.go` | May need minor updates for auth-aware operations | OCI filesystem |\n\n---\n\n## Reusable Patterns & Functions\n\n**From Git Storage (internal/storage/fs/git/)**:\n- Authentication struct pattern (BasicAuth, TokenAuth, Optional auth)\n- Validation pattern for auth type exclusivity\n- WithAuth() options pattern\n- Config-to-transport conversion pattern\n\n**From AWS S3 (internal/storage/fs/s3/)**:\n- AWS SDK v2 credential chain pattern: `config.LoadDefaultConfig(ctx, opts...)`\n- Options pattern for cloud-specific configuration\n\n**Existing Infrastructure**:\n- `containers.Option[T]` pattern (internal/containers/option.go)\n- Polling/Subscribe mechanism (internal/storage/fs/store.go)\n- ORAS library already in dependencies (oras.land/oras-go/v2 v2.3.1)\n\n---\n\n## Backward Compatibility\n\n- **Static credentials unchanged**: Existing OCI configs with basic auth continue to work\n- **No breaking changes**: New AWSAuth is optional, defaulting to no-auth behavior\n- **Gradual migration**: Users can switch from basic auth to AWS auth without downtime\n\n---\n\n## Verification\n\n1. **Existing tests pass**: Run `go test ./internal/config/...` and `go test ./internal/storage/fs/oci/...`\n2. **New tests for auth**: Unit tests for config validation, auth provider creation\n3. **Integration test**: Create a test that:\n   - Mocks AWS credentials provider\n   - Creates OCI source with AWS auth\n   - Verifies credentials are fetched\n   - Verifies Pull/Push operations work\n4. **Manual testing**: Deploy and test against real ECR registry (optional, for final validation)\n\n---\n\n## Key Dependencies Already Available\n\n- `github.com/aws/aws-sdk-go-v2` - AWS SDK v2 (already in go.mod)\n- `github.com/aws/aws-sdk-go-v2/config` - Credential chain support\n- `oras.land/oras-go/v2` - ORAS library with auth support\n- `github.com/opencontainers/image-spec` - OCI image spec\n\n---\n\n## Success Criteria\n\n1. \u2705 OCI storage supports static (username/password) authentication\n2. \u2705 OCI storage supports AWS credential chain authentication\n3. \u2705 Tokens refresh automatically on each poll interval\n4. \u2705 Configuration accepts new auth type selection\n5. \u2705 Backward compatibility maintained (static auth still works)\n6. \u2705 All existing tests pass\n7. \u2705 New tests cover auth functionality\n\n",

# Implementation Plan: Dynamic AWS ECR Authentication for OCI Bundles

## Context

**Problem**: Flipt configured with OCI storage cannot continuously pull bundles from AWS ECR when using temporary credentials. Only static `username/password` authentication is supported today; AWS-issued tokens expire (~12h), and after expiry, pulls fail until credentials are manually rotated.

**Solution Approach**: Add support for AWS credentials chain authentication in OCI storage, with automatic token refresh through periodic re-pulling (leveraging existing polling infrastructure).

**Scope**:
- Add authentication configuration options to OCI storage (static + AWS provider chain)
- Implement AWS ECR authentication using AWS SDK v2
- Leverage existing polling mechanism for automatic token refresh
- Maintain backward compatibility with static credentials
- Follow established Flipt patterns (Git storage auth as a model)

---

## Implementation Strategy

### Phase 1: Configuration Changes
**File**: `internal/config/storage.go`

1. **Extend OCI struct** to include authentication options (following Git storage pattern):
   - Add `Authentication` field to OCI struct
   - Define `OCIAuthentication` struct with:
     - `BasicAuth` (*BasicAuth) - for static username/password or ECR static credentials
     - `TokenAuth` (*TokenAuth) - for bearer tokens
     - `AWSAuth` (*AWSAuth) - NEW, for AWS credential chain (ECR)

2. **Define AWSAuth struct** with:
   ```go
   type AWSAuth struct {
       Region       string  // Optional, auto-detected if not provided
       UseChain     bool    // If true, use AWS credential chain (env vars, IAM role, etc.)
   }
   ```

3. **Add validation** for auth exclusivity (only one auth type at a time)

4. **Add setDefaults** for OCI polling interval (similar to S3)
... (truncated)
